  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12390099805803144204">30.	The new baby by Mayer Mercer <br />Genre:	fiction, children’s literature 	Reading level:age 3 and up	Format: good <br /><br /><br />The new baby is a book about the little critter that is super excited for the new baby at his home. So he tries doing things with his baby sister that makes him upset and sad because his baby sister doesn’t laugh at his funny jokes or pays attention at his stories. He then asks his mother what he can do to make his baby sister happy. His mother tells him to play with her rattle or rock her in her crib so she can fall asleep. The little critter then notices his baby sister is special. The picture illustrations are cute and enjoyable because the characters are different to other books. As I was reading the story I was smiling because it was nice seeing the picture illustrations relating to the text in the book. Since I was able to visualize how the little critter felt throughout the whole story. This book can be used in the classroom to teach students how delicate babies are. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11166856139396839506">I choose this book out of all the preparing for a new baby books because it is with a character that is already familiar to so many children. The well loved little critter gets a new baby sister. My favorite thing about this book is it isn't perfect from the start.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText11166856139396839506">I choose this book out of all the preparing for a new baby books because it is with a character that is already familiar to so many children. The well loved little critter gets a new baby sister. My favorite thing about this book is it isn't perfect from the start. Little critter tried reading to the new baby she doesn't listen, he tries making funny faces and she cries, he doesn't know what to do with the new baby and is having trouble dealing with it. But finally he finds what he can do with a baby and learns how to be a big brother! I don't have children of my own but I have watched families for years who have gone through this multiple times, they actually have this book and from what I viewed it was a great contribution to the situation. It is a hard change for a child especially if they are use to being the only one and I think it is important that this book shows that it can be hard, and you can cry, but also shows what great and fun things you can do when the baby comes and how cool it will be to be a big brother or sister.</span>

            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/46310567-caitlyn-nicole?shelf=beginning-books" class="actionLinkLite">beginning-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1439687382">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12094245271663162159">Mayer, Mercer. (1999). The New Baby (Little Critter). New York:Golden Books Publishing Company, Inc.<br />Setting: Little critter's home<br />Genre: Beginning Books for children<br /><br />In this charming story, little critter becomes a big brother. He doesn't know how to handle the idea of mommy having a baby. I would read this book in class for a Pre-K class because most parents have their second child after their first enters school. This book has not won any awards. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1195468758">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1195468758" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/39123771-emily" class="left imgcol" title="Emily"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1421176782p2/39123771.jpg" alt="Emily" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1195468758?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 09, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/39123771-emily" class="user" title="Emily">Emily</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/39123771-emily?shelf=picture-book" class="actionLinkLite">picture-book</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/39123771-emily?shelf=contemporary-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/39123771-emily?shelf=animals" class="actionLinkLite">animals</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1195468758">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6436952096803520817">A new baby is a lot to take in! Critter tries to do some of his favorite things with the baby, like read comic books, but the new baby doesn't seem to notice. Eventually he realizes that new babies can't do all the same things that big kids can do, but there are special things that you can do to play with new babies. This book is perfect for talking about differences between babies and grown kids, helping them prepare for new life in their families!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a href="/review/list/39471617-kelly-workman?shelf=el-230-goodreads-assignment" class="actionLinkLite">el-230-goodreads-assignment</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1211677213">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15697500928515804054">This book is a wonderful book that teaches children who are new to being older siblings that babies may be a handful, but they are worth it in the end. It is also good for children who are younger siblings, to help them understand their older siblings' frustrations. I gave this book three stars because, as a future teacher, this would not be much help in the classroom. I do, however, recommend this book for parents.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/534262926?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 12, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5049569-meghan-hunt" class="user" title="Meghan Hunt">Meghan Hunt</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5049569-meghan-hunt?shelf=jp-picture-books" class="actionLinkLite">jp-picture-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer534262926">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9816877885124078646">A little boy finds out that his family is bringing home a new baby sister for him. He gets out all of his favorite toys to share with her, but when she arrives she has no interest in them. He struggles to find what you can actually do with a new baby. He soon realizes that there are lots of things they can do like make her laugh by tickling her tummy, cuddling, and playing with a rattle. He soon becomes very proud of his baby sister.<br /><br />Great book for kids that are getting a new sibling.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_170428768">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170428768" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/42679-jacky" class="left imgcol" title="jacky"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1358794279p2/42679.jpg" alt="jacky" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/170428768?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 23, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/42679-jacky" class="user" title="jacky">jacky</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/42679-jacky?shelf=picture-books" class="actionLinkLite">picture-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/42679-jacky?shelf=lib-lew" class="actionLinkLite">lib-lew</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/42679-jacky?shelf=baby-prep" class="actionLinkLite">baby-prep</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer170428768">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12121992433747189130">This has been a favorite baby prep book for me so far, though Natalie didn't react too much. I guess her Critter phase is over for the time being. Anyway, it gives a pretty realistic view of how a toddler would react to a new baby. At first, Critter is excited and wants to play. Then, he is let down by the crying and smelliness. But, in the end he starts to see the things he can do with the baby and think about the future. Its a nice blend of emotions, all of which are realistic. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/692.Mercer_Mayer">About Mercer Mayer</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/692.Mercer_Mayer"><img alt="692" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1245185581p2/692.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer10149367956957379711">I began illustrating books in 1966. Since that time I have published over 300 books. Most of my books are about things that happened to me when I was a little kid. Now I'm a big kid and I write about things that happen now, especially with my own children. They always remind me of what it was like.<br /><br />I was born in Arkansas in 1943. Boy, that was a long time ago! It's real fun to be an old kid. Then m</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10149367956957379711">I began illustrating books in 1966. Since that time I have published over 300 books. Most of my books are about things that happened to me when I was a little kid. Now I'm a big kid and I write about things that happen now, especially with my own children. They always remind me of what it was like.<br /><br />I was born in Arkansas in 1943. Boy, that was a long time ago! It's real fun to be an old kid. Then my parents moved to Hawaii when I was thirteen years old. After High School, I went to Honolulu Academy of Arts. Then I moved to New York City. My wife, Gina, and I write the Little Critter stories together.<br /><br />For more information, please see <a rel="nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercer_Mayer" target="_blank">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercer_M...</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10149367956957379711">...more</a>

    </div>
